The Meridian Circle
Al-Taftazani defines the meridian circle and its function.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of the meridian circle, its poles, and its role in determining solar and stellar altitudes.

Core Idea
The meridian circle bisects the equator and marks noon.

Al-Taftazani now defines the meridian circle, which passes through the zenith and nadir and is named for its role in marking midday. He also notes a limitation of the definition and describes how the meridian helps determine celestial positions.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of the meridian
Find what the meridian circle is and through which points it passes. Note its name and the reason.
It is a great circle through the zenith and nadir.
2
Note the caveat about the definition
The author says the definition is not universal. Understand why: it could apply to any circle through the world's poles when they are at zenith/nadir.
This occurs only when the horizon coincides with the equator.
3
Identify the meridian's poles and function
The meridian has its own poles (east and west points) and it bisects the equator and daily paths. It is used to find maximum altitudes and depressions.
This is crucial for astronomy and timekeeping.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قطبي العالم انطبقت دائرة الأفق على معدل النهار وكان الدور رحويا وذلك حيث يكون أحد قطبي العالم على سمت الرأس وإن كانا غير قطبي العالم كان الأفق مقاطعا لمعدل النهار على نقطتين تسمى إحداهما نقطة المشرق ومطلع الاعتدال ووسط المشارق والأخرى نقطة المغرب ومغرب الاعتدال ووسط المغارب وتقاطعهما إن كان على زوايا قوائم سمي الأفق أفق الاستواء وإلا فالأفق الماثل ولا حصر للآفاق الماثلة ومنها دائرة نصف النهار وهي عظيمة تمر بقطبي الأفق أعني سمت الرأس والقدم ولقطبي العالم سميت بذلك لأن النهار ينتصف عند وصول الشمس إليها ولا خفاء في عدم اطراد التعريف إذ قد يصدق على كل دائرة تمر بقطبي العالم عند كونهما سمتي الرأس والقدم أعني حيث ينطبق دائرة الأفق على معدل النهار وهذه الدائرة قطباها نقطتا المشرق والمغرب وهي تنصف المعدل والمدارات اليومية الظاهرة منها والخفية وبها يعرف غاية ارتفاع الشمس والكواكب وذلك حين يصل إليها فوق الأرض وغاية انحطاطها وذلك إذا وصلت إليها تحت الأرض
When the two poles of the world, the circle of the horizon coincides with the celestial equator, and the revolution is spherical; this is when one of the two poles of the world is at the zenith. If they are not the poles of the world, the horizon intersects the celestial equator at two points: one called the point of the east, the rising of the equinox, and the middle of the risings; the other is the point of the west, the setting of the equinox, and the middle of the settings. If their intersection is at right angles, the horizon is called the horizon of the equator; otherwise it is the inclined horizon. There is no limit to the inclined horizons. Among them is the circle of the meridian, which is a great circle passing through the poles of the horizon, i.e., the zenith and nadir. It is named after the two poles of the world because the noon occurs when the sun reaches it. It is not hidden that the definition is not universal, for it may apply to any circle passing through the two poles of the world when they are the zenith and nadir, i.e., when the circle of the horizon coincides with the celestial equator. This circle has its two poles at the points of the east and west, and it bisects the equator and all the visible and invisible daily paths. By it the maximum altitude of the sun and stars is known, when it reaches above the earth, and their maximum depression, when it reaches below the earth.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage defines the celestial circles, specifically the horizon, equator, and meridian, in relation to the poles of the world. The author begins by describing the horizon relative to the celestial equator when the poles are aligned with the zenith. He then explains two types of horizon: the right horizon (when intersection is at right angles) and the inclined horizon. Next, he defines the meridian circle, which passes through the zenith and nadir, and is named because noon occurs when the sun reaches it. The author notes a lack of universal definition for this term. Finally, he describes the meridian's poles (east and west points) and its function in determining solar and stellar altitudes and depressions.

Key Terms
نصف النهار
سمت الرأس
سمت القدم
قطبا الأفق
نقطة المشرق
نقطة المغرب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The meridian circle always passes through the world's poles.
Correction: It passes through the poles of the horizon (zenith and nadir), not necessarily the world's poles; the world's poles are on it only when the horizon coincides with the equator.

Checkpoint
Through which points does the meridian circle always pass?
A) The north and south celestial poles
B) The east and west points
C) The zenith and nadir
D) The rising and setting points of the sun

Key Takeaway
The meridian circle, passing through the zenith and nadir, is essential for determining noon and the maximum altitudes of celestial bodies.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The meridian marks the exact moment of noon, a daily appointment with your Creator. When the sun stands directly overhead in your own meridian, do you use that moment to pause and renew your covenant with Allah, or do you let it pass unnoticed? Commit today to making the call to Dhuhr a trigger for sincere, present-moment worship, as if you are standing on the edge of the Divine Horizon.
?
The meridian is defined relative to your location—it changes as you move. Reflect: Are your spiritual priorities fixed on an absolute standard (the Qur'an and Sunnah) or are they shifting with the whims of your 'horizon'—your culture, desires, or comfort? Ask yourself: am I willing to correct my personal 'meridian' to align with Allah's guidance, even if it means reorienting my entire daily life?
?
The source notes that the meridian bisects the equator and every daily path, revealing the maximum height a star can reach. In your own spiritual journey, what is the 'maximum altitude' you aim for in sincerity, taqwa, and knowledge of Allah? Have you settled for mediocrity? Write down one concrete step to raise that ceiling this week.

The Three Celestial Circles That Divide the Earth
Al-Taftazani enumerates the three circles and their divisions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the three celestial circles—the equator, the horizon of the equator, and the meridian—divide the earth into hemispheres and quarters.

Core Idea
The earth is divided by three circles into northern/southern, visible/hidden, and eastern/western halves.

Al-Taftazani begins by explaining that great Islamic geographers have projected key celestial circles onto the earth's surface. These three imaginary circles—the equator, the horizon of the equator, and the meridian—serve as fundamental reference lines for dividing the globe into distinct regions. Understanding these divisions is essential for locating places and determining their climatic zones.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the three circles
Read the Arabic passage once to get the overall description of the three circles and their divisions.
Notice that the author uses a clear enumerative structure.
2
Identify each circle and its dividing role
Find the three circles: the equator (dividing north/south), the horizon of the equator (dividing visible/hidden), and the meridian (dividing east/west).
The second circle has multiple names.
3
Understand the concept of the inhabited quarter
The passage mentions that the northern visible quarter is called the inhabited part (al-ma'mura), though much of it is ruined.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وتوهموا في سطح كل من معدل النهار وأفق الاستواء ونصف النهار دائرة على الأرض فانقسمت بالأولى ويسمى خط الاستواء إلى جنوبي وشمالي وبالثانية إلى ظاهر وخفي والمكشوف أحد الربعين الشماليين ويسمى المعمورة وبالثالثة إلى شرقي وغربي بأن جعلوا الدوائر الثلاث قاطعة للعالم فلا محالة يحدث على بسيط الأرض ثلاث دوائر إحداها تسمى خط الاستواء وخط الاعتدال وهو الفاصل بين النصف الجنوبي من الأرض والشمالي منها والثانية تسمى أفق خط الاستواء وأفق نصف نهار القبة وأفق وسط الأرض وهو الفاصل بين النصف الظاهر من الأرض والنصف الخفي وبهاتين الدائرتين تصير الأرض أرباعا والمكشوف منها أحد الربعين الشماليين وتسمى المعمورة والربع المسكون وإن كان أكثره خرابا والثالثة تسمى خط نصف النهار وهو الفاصل بين النصف الشرقي من الأرض والغربي منها قال وسموا من دائرة نصف النهار ما بين سمت الرأس البلد ومعدل النهار عرض البلد ومن معدل النهار ما بين نصف نهار البلد ونصف نهار آخر العمارة في الغرب طول البلد عرض البلد قوس من دائرة نصف النهار ما بين معدل النهار وقطب أفق البلد أعني سمت الرأس ولا محالة تساوي ما بين أفق البلد وقطب المعدل أعني ارتفاع القطب ففي أفق الاستواء لا عرض للبلد لأن الخط الخارج من مركز العالم المار بسمتي الرأس والقدم يقع على معدل النهار ولا يبعد عنه وفي الأفق المنطبق على معدل النهار يكون العرض في الغاية أعني تسعين وفي غيرهما يكون للبلد عرض بقدر ميل الأفق عن المعدل فإذا كان له عرض بقدر ميل الأفق عن المعدل فإذا رأسه في السنة مرتين عنه كون الشمس في رأس الجبل والميزان ثم مالت منه نحو الشمال ونحو الجنوب بمقدار واحد ويسمى خط الاستواء والاعتداد بسبب تساوي النهار والليل فقط
He said: And they imagined on the surface of each of the celestial equator, the horizon of the equator, and the meridian a circle on the earth. So it divided by the first, called the equator, into southern and northern; by the second into apparent and hidden, and the uncovered is one of the two northern quarters, called the inhabited part; and by the third into eastern and western. Because they made the three circles intersecting the world, inevitably there occur on the earth's surface three circles: one called the equator and the equinoctial line, which is the separator between the southern half of the earth and its northern; the second called the horizon of the equator, the horizon of the meridian of the dome, and the horizon of the middle of the earth, which is the separator between the apparent half of the earth and the hidden half; and by these two circles the earth becomes quarters, and the uncovered of them is one of the two northern quarters, called the inhabited part and the inhabited quarter, even if most of it is ruined; and the third called the line of the meridian, which is the separator between the eastern half of the earth and its western. He said: And they named from the circle of the meridian the arc between the zenith of the country and the celestial equator the latitude of the country; and from the celestial equator the arc between the meridian of the country and the meridian of the other inhabited area in the west the longitude of the country. The latitude of the country is an arc of the meridian circle between the celestial equator and the pole of the horizon of the country, i.e., the zenith; and it inevitably equals the arc between the horizon of the country and the pole of the equator, i.e., the elevation of the pole. So on the horizon of the equator there is no latitude for the country, because the line exiting from the center of the world passing through the zenith and nadir falls on the celestial equator and does not depart from it; and on the horizon coinciding with the celestial equator the latitude is at the extreme, i.e., ninety; and in other cases the country has latitude equal to the inclination of the horizon from the equator. So if it has latitude equal to the inclination of the horizon from the equator, then its apex twice in the year concerning the sun being in the constellation of Aquila and the Scales, then it inclines from it towards the north and towards the south by equal amount, and it is called the equator and the equinox because of the equality of day and night only.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage explains the division of the earth by three celestial circles and defines latitude. The author begins by describing how three imaginary circles on the earth's surface are derived from projecting the celestial equator, the horizon of the equator, and the meridian onto the earth. The first circle, the equator, divides the earth into southern and northern halves. The second, the horizon of the equator, divides the earth into apparent and hidden halves, and the uncovered northern quarter is called the inhabited part (al-ma'mura). The third, the meridian, divides the earth into eastern and western halves. The author then defines the latitude of a country as the arc of the meridian between the celestial equator and the zenith; longitude is also defined. He explains that when the horizon coincides with the equator, latitude is zero or ninety, and otherwise it equals the inclination of the horizon from the equator. The concluding sentence mentions the sun passing over the equator twice a year, leading to equinoxes.

Key Terms
خط الاستواء
أفق الاستواء
خط نصف النهار
المعمورة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The horizon of the equator is the same as the terrestrial horizon.
Correction: The horizon of the equator is specifically the great circle intersecting the celestial equator at the observer's location, not the local horizon.

Checkpoint
What does the second circle, called the horizon of the equator, separate?
A) Southern and northern halves
B) Eastern and western halves
C) Apparent and hidden halves
D) The inhabited and uninhabited parts

Key Takeaway
Three celestial circles projected onto the earth define the fundamental divisions of the globe into hemispheres and quarters.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Reflect on the precision with which early scholars mapped the world using celestial references. How does this attention to detail challenge your own approach to seeking knowledge? Are you satisfied with superficial understanding, or are you willing to dig deep like these scholars?
?
The inhabited quarter (al-ma'mura) is described as 'mostly ruined' even though it is called inhabited. How does this reality check your assumptions about prosperity and divine favor? Does this make you reconsider what true prosperity means in your own life?
?
These divisions show that our perspective is limited to one quarter of the earth. How does this humbling spatial awareness affect your view of your place in Allah's creation? Are you content with your limited view, or does it drive you to seek a broader understanding of His signs?

Defining Latitude and Longitude
Al-Taftazani defines latitude and longitude using celestial arcs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how latitude and longitude are defined in terms of celestial circles: latitude as the arc from the equator to the zenith, and longitude as the arc along the equator between meridians.

Core Idea
Latitude is measured from the equator to the zenith; longitude is measured along the equator between meridians.

Having established the three great circles, al-Taftazani now defines the two coordinates that locate any place on earth: latitude and longitude. Latitude is the arc of the meridian between the celestial equator and the local zenith, while longitude is the arc along the equator between the local meridian and the prime meridian (or the meridian of the furthest inhabited point westward). These definitions rely on the same celestial projections.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of latitude and longitude
Read the passage carefully, noting how each coordinate is defined as an arc on the celestial sphere.
Pay attention to the terms 'سمت الرأس' (zenith) and 'معدل النهار' (celestial equator).
2
Understand latitude as the arc from equator to zenith
Latitude is the arc of the meridian between the celestial equator and the zenith. It equals the elevation of the pole above the horizon.
3
Understand longitude as the arc along the equator between meridians
Longitude is the arc along the celestial equator between the local meridian and the meridian of the westernmost inhabited area.
This definition differs from modern prime meridian conventions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وتوهموا في سطح كل من معدل النهار وأفق الاستواء ونصف النهار دائرة على الأرض فانقسمت بالأولى ويسمى خط الاستواء إلى جنوبي وشمالي وبالثانية إلى ظاهر وخفي والمكشوف أحد الربعين الشماليين ويسمى المعمورة وبالثالثة إلى شرقي وغربي بأن جعلوا الدوائر الثلاث قاطعة للعالم فلا محالة يحدث على بسيط الأرض ثلاث دوائر إحداها تسمى خط الاستواء وخط الاعتدال وهو الفاصل بين النصف الجنوبي من الأرض والشمالي منها والثانية تسمى أفق خط الاستواء وأفق نصف نهار القبة وأفق وسط الأرض وهو الفاصل بين النصف الظاهر من الأرض والنصف الخفي وبهاتين الدائرتين تصير الأرض أرباعا والمكشوف منها أحد الربعين الشماليين وتسمى المعمورة والربع المسكون وإن كان أكثره خرابا والثالثة تسمى خط نصف النهار وهو الفاصل بين النصف الشرقي من الأرض والغربي منها قال وسموا من دائرة نصف النهار ما بين سمت الرأس البلد ومعدل النهار عرض البلد ومن معدل النهار ما بين نصف نهار البلد ونصف نهار آخر العمارة في الغرب طول البلد عرض البلد قوس من دائرة نصف النهار ما بين معدل النهار وقطب أفق البلد أعني سمت الرأس ولا محالة تساوي ما بين أفق البلد وقطب المعدل أعني ارتفاع القطب ففي أفق الاستواء لا عرض للبلد لأن الخط الخارج من مركز العالم المار بسمتي الرأس والقدم يقع على معدل النهار ولا يبعد عنه وفي الأفق المنطبق على معدل النهار يكون العرض في الغاية أعني تسعين وفي غيرهما يكون للبلد عرض بقدر ميل الأفق عن المعدل فإذا كان له عرض بقدر ميل الأفق عن المعدل فإذا رأسه في السنة مرتين عنه كون الشمس في رأس الجبل والميزان ثم مالت منه نحو الشمال ونحو الجنوب بمقدار واحد ويسمى خط الاستواء والاعتداد بسبب تساوي النهار والليل فقط

So it divided by the first, called the equator, into southern and northern; by the second into apparent and hidden, and the uncovered is one of the two northern quarters, called the inhabited part; and by the third into eastern and western. ?

?

?
Latitude equals the elevation of the pole—a hidden constant that determines your position. What hidden habits or assumptions in your life are shaping your spiritual 'latitude'? Will you consciously examine and adjust them today?

5 min
Latitude at the Equator and Poles, and the Equinox
Al-Taftazani explains extreme latitudes and the equinox.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why latitude is zero at the equator, ninety degrees at the pole, and how the sun's passage over the equator creates the equinox.

Core Idea
At the equator latitude is zero, at the pole it's 90; the sun crosses the equator twice yearly causing equal day and night.

Al-Taftazani now explains two special cases: the equator where the zenith lies on the celestial equator giving zero latitude, and the pole where the horizon aligns with the equator giving maximum latitude of 90 degrees. He then connects these concepts to the sun's annual motion, noting that when the sun is at the equinoctial points, it passes directly over the equator, resulting in equal day and night worldwide.

Guided Path
1
Read about zero latitude at the equator
The passage explains that on the horizon of the equator, the zenith lies on the equator, so latitude is zero.
2
Read about 90-degree latitude at the pole
When the horizon coincides with the celestial equator, latitude is at its maximum of 90 degrees.
3
Understand the link to the equinox
The sun passes over the equator twice a year, resulting in equal day and night. After that, it inclines north and south.
The constellations mentioned (Aquila and al-Mizan) correspond to the equinoctial points.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وتوهموا في سطح كل من معدل النهار وأفق الاستواء ونصف النهار دائرة على الأرض فانقسمت بالأولى ويسمى خط الاستواء إلى جنوبي وشمالي وبالثانية إلى ظاهر وخفي والمكشوف أحد الربعين الشماليين ويسمى المعمورة وبالثالثة إلى شرقي وغربي بأن جعلوا الدوائر الثلاث قاطعة للعالم فلا محالة يحدث على بسيط الأرض ثلاث دوائر إحداها تسمى خط الاستواء وخط الاعتدال وهو الفاصل بين النصف الجنوبي من الأرض والشمالي منها والثانية تسمى أفق خط الاستواء وأفق نصف نهار القبة وأفق وسط الأرض وهو الفاصل بين النصف الظاهر من الأرض والنصف الخفي وبهاتين الدائرتين تصير الأرض أرباعا والمكشوف منها أحد الربعين الشماليين وتسمى المعمورة والربع المسكون وإن كان أكثره خرابا والثالثة تسمى خط نصف النهار وهو الفاصل بين النصف الشرقي من الأرض والغربي منها قال وسموا من دائرة نصف النهار ما بين سمت الرأس البلد ومعدل النهار عرض البلد ومن معدل النهار ما بين نصف نهار البلد ونصف نهار آخر العمارة في الغرب طول البلد عرض البلد قوس من دائرة نصف النهار ما بين معدل النهار وقطب أفق البلد أعني سمت الرأس ولا محالة تساوي ما بين أفق البلد وقطب المعدل أعني ارتفاع القطب ففي أفق الاستواء لا عرض للبلد لأن الخط الخارج من مركز العالم المار بسمتي الرأس والقدم يقع على معدل النهار ولا يبعد عنه وفي الأفق المنطبق على معدل النهار يكون العرض في الغاية أعني تسعين وفي غيرهما يكون للبلد عرض بقدر ميل الأفق عن المعدل فإذا كان له عرض بقدر ميل الأفق عن المعدل فإذا رأسه في السنة مرتين عنه كون الشمس في رأس الجبل والميزان ثم مالت منه نحو الشمال ونحو الجنوب بمقدار واحد ويسمى خط الاستواء والاعتداد بسبب تساوي النهار والليل فقط
He said: And they imagined on the surface of each of the celestial equator, the horizon of the equator, and the meridian a circle on the earth. So it divided by the first, called the equator, into southern and northern; by the second into apparent and hidden, and the uncovered is one of the two northern quarters, called the inhabited part; and by the third into eastern and western. Because they made the three circles intersecting the world, inevitably there occur on the earth's surface three circles: one called the equator and the equinoctial line, which is the separator between the southern half of the earth and its northern; the second called the horizon of the equator, the horizon of the meridian of the dome, and the horizon of the middle of the earth, which is the separator between the apparent half of the earth and the hidden half; and by these two circles the earth becomes quarters, and the uncovered of them is one of the two northern quarters, called the inhabited part and the inhabited quarter, even if most of it is ruined; and the third called the line of the meridian, which is the separator between the eastern half of the earth and its western. He said: And they named from the circle of the meridian the arc between the zenith of the country and the celestial equator the latitude of the country; and from the celestial equator the arc between the meridian of the country and the meridian of the other inhabited area in the west the longitude of the country. The latitude of the country is an arc of the meridian circle between the celestial equator and the pole of the horizon of the country, i.e., the zenith; and it inevitably equals the arc between the horizon of the country and the pole of the equator, i.e., the elevation of the pole. So on the horizon of the equator there is no latitude for the country, because the line exiting from the center of the world passing through the zenith and nadir falls on the celestial equator and does not depart from it; and on the horizon coinciding with the celestial equator the latitude is at the extreme, i.e., ninety; and in other cases the country has latitude equal to the inclination of the horizon from the equator. So if it has latitude equal to the inclination of the horizon from the equator, then its apex twice in the year concerning the sun being in the constellation of Aquila and the Scales, then it inclines from it towards the north and towards the south by equal amount, and it is called the equator and the equinox because of the equality of day and night only.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage explains the division of the earth by three celestial circles and defines latitude. The author begins by describing how three imaginary circles on the earth's surface are derived from projecting the celestial equator, the horizon of the equator, and the meridian onto the earth. The first circle, the equator, divides the earth into southern and northern halves. The second, the horizon of the equator, divides the earth into apparent and hidden halves, and the uncovered northern quarter is called the inhabited part (al-ma'mura). The third, the meridian, divides the earth into eastern and western halves. The author then defines the latitude of a country as the arc of the meridian between the celestial equator and the zenith; longitude is also defined. He explains that when the horizon coincides with the equator, latitude is zero or ninety, and otherwise it equals the inclination of the horizon from the equator. The concluding sentence mentions the sun passing over the equator twice a year, leading to equinoxes.

Key Terms
أفق الاستواء
ارتفاع القطب
الاعتدال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The sun always rises due east everywhere.
Correction: Only at the equator does the sun rise due east; at other latitudes, the rising point shifts due to the sun's declination.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does the sun pass directly over the equator?
A) Once a year
B) Twice a year
C) Every month
D) Never

Key Takeaway
Latitude ranges from 0° at the equator to 90° at the poles; the sun crosses the equator twice a year causing equinoxes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The sun's crossing of the equator twice a year is so precise that day and night become equal. Have you ever taken a moment to watch the sunrise or sunset on the equinox and reflect on the perfect order of Allah's creation? What keeps you from pausing to contemplate His signs regularly? Commit to observing the next equinox with intentional gratitude.
?
Every place on Earth has a specific latitude, and that determines the sun's path, the seasons, and the length of day. Your own location is not random—it is part of Allah's decree. How does knowing that your specific place has been chosen for you affect your sense of purpose and your relationship with your local environment? What is one way you can better appreciate the signs of Allah in your own backyard starting today?
?
The equinox is a moment of balance—day and night are equal. Your own life may feel unbalanced, with too much focus on one aspect over another. In light of the perfect order of the cosmos, what specific imbalance will you address this week? Write down one action you will take to restore equilibrium in your daily routine, and ask Allah to help you maintain it.

The Three Circles Dividing the Earth
Explains the three circles that divide the earth into quarters.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how three circles—the equator, the horizon of the equator, and the meridian—divide the earth into quarters and how the inhabited region is defined.

Core Idea
Two circles quarter the Earth; a third separates east from west.

This passage from the text explains a foundational geographical concept used in classical cosmology. The scholars identified three key circles on the globe that help define hemispheres and quarters, setting the stage for calculations of latitude, longitude, and inhabited regions. Let's explore these circles one by one.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and then the literal English translation. Familiarize yourself with the terminology for each circle.
Notice that the second circle has multiple names.
2
Identify the first two circles
The equator and the horizon of the equator together divide the earth into four quarters. Understand how each circle functions as a separator.
The horizon of the equator is also called the horizon of the celestial meridian or the middle horizon.
3
Understand the third circle and the inhabited quarter
The meridian separates the eastern and western halves. The exposed quarter is one of the two northern quarters, called the inhabited region, though most of it is ruined.
This clarifies the geographical scope of human habitation—it is not fully populated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بأن جعلوا الدوائر الثلاث قاطعة للعالم فلا محالة يحدث على بسيط الأرض ثلاث دوائر، إحداها تسمى خط الاستواء، وخط الاعتدال وهو الفاصل بين النصف الجنوبي من الأرض والشمالي منها، والثانية تسمى أفق خط الاستواء وأفق نصف نهار القبة، وأفق وسط الأرض، وهو الفاصل بين النصف الظاهر من الأرض، والنصف الخفي، وبهاتين الدائرتين تصير الأرض أرباعاً، والمكشوف منها أحد الربعين الشماليين، وتسمى المعمورة والربع المسكون، وإن كان أكثره خراباً. والثالثة تسمى خط نصف النهار، وهو الفاصل بين النصف الشرقي من الأرض والغربي منها.
That they made the three circles intersecting the globe inevitably produce on the surface of the earth three circles: one is called the equator and the line of equinox, which is the separator between the southern and northern halves of the earth; the second is called the horizon of the equator, the horizon of the celestial meridian, and the horizon of the middle of the earth, and it is the separator between the visible and hidden halves of the earth; and by these two circles the earth becomes quarters, and the exposed part is one of the two northern quarters, called the inhabited region and the inhabited quarter, even though most of it is ruined. The third is called the meridian line, which is the separator between the eastern and western halves of the earth.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage describes the three fundamental circles used by geographers to divide the earth into hemispheres and quarters. It begins by stating that scholars have established three intersecting circles on the globe. The first is the equator, also called the line of equinox, which separates the northern and southern hemispheres. The second is the horizon of the equator, also referred to as the horizon of the celestial meridian or the middle horizon, which divides the earth into visible and hidden halves. Together with the equator, these two circles divide the earth into four quarters. The exposed quarter is one of the two northern quarters, called the inhabited region (al-ma'mura) or the inhabited quarter, even though much of it is not actually inhabited. The third circle is the meridian, which separates the eastern and western halves. This division sets the stage for further geographical calculations such as latitude and longitude.

Key Terms
خط الاستواء
خط الاعتدال
أفق خط الاستواء
أفق نصف نهار القبة
أفق وسط الأرض
خط نصف النهار
المعمورة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The inhabited quarter is fully populated and comprises the entire habitable world.
Correction: The text clarifies that most of the inhabited quarter is ruined, so it is not entirely populated.

Checkpoint
What is the function of the third circle described in this passage?
A) It separates the northern and southern hemispheres.
B) It divides the earth into visible and hidden halves.
C) It separates the eastern and western halves of the earth.
D) It defines the inhabited region.

Key Takeaway
Three circles—equator, horizon of equator, and meridian—divide the earth into quarters and hemispheres; the inhabited quarter is a northern quarter, mostly ruined.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The text says that even the inhabited quarter is mostly ruined. If the world's built environment is mostly decay, what does that mean for your ambitions and dreams rooted in this world? Are you investing in what lasts?
?
The horizon of the equator separates what is visible from what is hidden. In your own life, what parts of your spiritual state are currently hidden from you? What would it take to bring them to light?
?
The earth is divided into quarters, but only one is considered inhabited. In the grand scheme of creation, your life occupies a tiny fraction. Does this perspective shift your priorities? What one change can you make today to live more for the Hereafter?

Latitude and Longitude Defined
Defines latitude and longitude with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how latitude and longitude are defined in Islamic geography and how they are calculated using celestial references.

Core Idea
Latitude is distance from the equator; longitude is time difference from the west.

Before we explore the seven climes, we must understand how geographers located places. This passage defines latitude and longitude using the meridian, celestial equator, and solar observations. These definitions are essential for mapping the inhabited world.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage on latitude and longitude
Read the passage from 'قال وسموا' to the end of the longitude definition. Note the technical terms: معدل النهار, سمت الرأس, etc.
Focus on the definitions and the method for calculating latitude.
2
Understand the definition of latitude
Latitude is the arc between the celestial equator and the zenith, equal to the elevation of the pole. It is zero at the equator and ninety at the pole. The calculation method: measure the sun's altitude at equinox noon and subtract from ninety.
3
Understand the definition of longitude
Longitude is the arc between the town's meridian and the meridian of the westernmost habitation. The Greeks used the west as baseline, with varying definitions for the western boundary.
The difference between the two boundaries is ten degrees or about 220 parasangs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وسموا من دائرة نصف النهار وما بين سمت الرأس البلد، ومعدل النهار عرض البلد، ومن معدل النهار، ما نصف نهار البلد، ونصف نهار آخر العمارة في الغرب بطول البلد. عرض البلد قوس من دائرة نصف النهار ما بين معدل النهار، وقطب أفق البلد. أعني سمت الرأس، ولا محالة تساوي ما بين أفق البلد، وقطب المعدل أعني ارتفاع القطب، ففي أفق الاستواء لا عرض للبلد، لأن الخط الخارج من مركز العالم المار بسمتي الرأس، والقدم يقع على معدل النهار، ولا يبعد عنه، وفي الأفق المنطبق على معدل النهار يكون العرض في الغاية. أعني تسعين، وفي غيرهما يكون للبلد عرض بقدر ميل الأفق عن المعدل، فإذا أخذنا ارتفاع الشمس في نصف النهار يوم الاعتدال الربيعي أو الخريفي وألقيناه من تسعين كان الباقي عرض البلد، وأما طول البلد فهو قوس من النهار ما بين نصف نهار البلد، ونصف نهار آخر العمارة في المغرب . واعتبر اليونانيون من المغرب، لكونه أقرب نهايتي العمارة إليهم ، وآخر العمارة عند بعضهم ساحل البحر الغربي، وعند بطليموس الجزائر الخالدات الواغلة في البحر، وبينهما عشر درجات وهي قريبة من مائتين وعشرين فرسخاً. قال وقسموا المعمورة سبع قطاع موازية لمعدل النهار ممتدة من المشرق إلى المغرب سموها الأقاليم السبعة. لما لم يكن على خط الاستواء وما يدانيه شمالاً وجنوباً عمارة وافرة لفرط الحرارة، ولم يكن حوالي القطبين عمارة أصلاً لفرط البرودة، وقع معظم العمارة في الربع المسكون بين ما يجاوز عشر درجات في العرض عن خط الاستواء إلى أن يبلغ العرض قريب خمسين، فقسم أهل الصناعة هذا القدر سبعة أقسام في العرض حسب ما ظهر لهم من تفاوت تشابه الأحوال في الحر والبرد، فاعتبروا في الطول الامتداد من المشرق إلى المغرب، وفي العرض تفاضل نصف ساعة في مقادير النهار الأطول أعني نهار كون الشمس في الانقلاب الصيفي، وكل من الأقاليم ينحصر بين نصفي مدارين موازيين لخط الاستواء أشبه شيء بأنصاف
He said: And they called from the meridian and what is between the zenith direction of the town and the celestial equator the latitude of the town, and from the celestial equator what is the meridian of the town and the meridian of the furthest habitation in the west the longitude of the town. The latitude of the town is an arc of the meridian between the celestial equator and the pole of the horizon of the town, i.e., the zenith, and it necessarily equals what is between the horizon of the town and the pole of the celestial equator, i.e., the elevation of the pole. So at the horizon of the equator, there is no latitude for the town because the line from the center of the world passing through the two zeniths of the head and the foot falls on the celestial equator and does not depart from it. At the horizon coinciding with the celestial equator, the latitude is at its maximum, i.e., ninety. In other cases, the town has a latitude equal to the inclination of the horizon from the celestial equator. So if we take the altitude of the sun at midday on the vernal or autumnal equinox and subtract it from ninety, the remainder is the latitude of the town. As for the longitude of the town, it is an arc of the day between the meridian of the town and the meridian of the furthest habitation in the west. The Greeks took the west as baseline because it was the closest of the two ends of habitation to them. The furthest habitation according to some is the western sea coast, and according to Ptolemy it is the eternal islands extending into the sea, with ten degrees between them, which is close to two hundred and twenty parasangs. He said: And they divided the inhabited region into seven zones parallel to the celestial equator extending from east to west, calling them the seven climes. Since there was not abundant habitation on the equator and its vicinity north and south due to excessive heat, and there was no habitation at all around the poles due to extreme cold, most habitation occurred in the inhabited quarter between what exceeds ten degrees in latitude from the equator until the latitude reaches about fifty. So the experts of the craft divided this amount into seven divisions in latitude according to what appeared to them of the variation in similarity of conditions in heat and cold. They considered in longitude the extension from east to west, and in latitude the difference of half an hour in the amounts of the longest day, i.e., the day when the sun is at the summer solstice. And each of the climes is bounded between two semicircles parallel to the equator, resembling semicircles
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage defines latitude and longitude and then explains the division of the inhabited world into seven climes. It begins by stating how latitude and longitude are derived from the meridian: latitude is the arc between the celestial equator and the zenith of the town, which equals the elevation of the pole. At the equator, latitude is zero; at the pole, it is ninety degrees. Latitude is calculated by measuring the sun's altitude at noon on an equinox and subtracting it from ninety. Longitude is the arc between the town's meridian and the meridian of the westernmost inhabited point; the Greeks used the western boundary because it was closer to them, with varying definitions (the western sea shore or Ptolemy's 'eternal islands'). The passage then transitions to the seven climes: because excessive heat near the equator and extreme cold near the poles prevent habitation, most of the inhabited world lies between roughly ten and fifty degrees latitude. Scholars divided this band into seven zones (aqalim) based on differences in climate and the duration of the longest day (summer solstice). Each clime is bounded by two parallel circles resembling semicircles. The passage ends mid-sentence but provides the key rationale and method.

Key Terms
عرض البلد
طول البلد
معدل النهار
سمت الرأس
قطب أفق البلد
ارتفاع القطب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Latitude and longitude are the same measurement.
Correction: Latitude measures north-south distance from the equator; longitude measures east-west time difference from a baseline meridian.

Checkpoint
How is the latitude of a town calculated according to this passage?
A) By measuring the length of the longest day.
B) By subtracting the sun's altitude at noon on an equinox from ninety degrees.
C) By measuring the distance from the equator in parasangs.
D) By comparing the meridian with the westernmost point.

Key Takeaway
Latitude is derived from the sun's equinox altitude, longitude from the difference in meridians with the west as baseline.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The author describes the precise method ancient scholars used to determine their place on Earth. In your daily life, what fixed points do you use to orient your actions and decisions? Are they as reliable as the celestial equator and equinox? If not, what would it take to establish such a foundation?
?
The scholars disagreed about the exact western boundary for measuring longitude. How often do you allow differing opinions about worldly matters to distract you from the clear, unchanging truths of the Qur'an and sunna? Write down one area where you need to stop disputing and start acting.

The Seven Climes of the Inhabited World
Explains the division of the inhabited world into seven climes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the inhabited world is divided into seven climes and how they are defined by latitude and day length.

Core Idea
The seven climes are climate zones based on latitude and the length of the longest day.

After defining latitude and longitude, al-Sanusi explains how scholars divided the habitable region into seven parallel zones. These climes are not political but climatic, determined by heat, cold, and the variation in daylight hours.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the seven climes
Read from 'قال وقسموا المعمورة' to the end. Notice the reasoning based on temperature extremes and the use of the longest day length.
The passage ends mid-sentence, but the key ideas are complete.
2
Understand the rationale for the climes
The equator and poles are uninhabitable due to excessive heat and cold. Most habitation lies between roughly 10° and 50° latitude.
3
Understand the division criteria
The climes are divided by half-hour differences in the length of the longest day (summer solstice). Each clime is bounded by two parallels.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وسموا من دائرة نصف النهار وما بين سمت الرأس البلد، ومعدل النهار عرض البلد، ومن معدل النهار، ما نصف نهار البلد، ونصف نهار آخر العمارة في الغرب بطول البلد. عرض البلد قوس من دائرة نصف النهار ما بين معدل النهار، وقطب أفق البلد. أعني سمت الرأس، ولا محالة تساوي ما بين أفق البلد، وقطب المعدل أعني ارتفاع القطب، ففي أفق الاستواء لا عرض للبلد، لأن الخط الخارج من مركز العالم المار بسمتي الرأس، والقدم يقع على معدل النهار، ولا يبعد عنه، وفي الأفق المنطبق على معدل النهار يكون العرض في الغاية. أعني تسعين، وفي غيرهما يكون للبلد عرض بقدر ميل الأفق عن المعدل، فإذا أخذنا ارتفاع الشمس في نصف النهار يوم الاعتدال الربيعي أو الخريفي وألقيناه من تسعين كان الباقي عرض البلد، وأما طول البلد فهو قوس من النهار ما بين نصف نهار البلد، ونصف نهار آخر العمارة في المغرب . واعتبر اليونانيون من المغرب، لكونه أقرب نهايتي العمارة إليهم ، وآخر العمارة عند بعضهم ساحل البحر الغربي، وعند بطليموس الجزائر الخالدات الواغلة في البحر، وبينهما عشر درجات وهي قريبة من مائتين وعشرين فرسخاً. قال وقسموا المعمورة سبع قطاع موازية لمعدل النهار ممتدة من المشرق إلى المغرب سموها الأقاليم السبعة. لما لم يكن على خط الاستواء وما يدانيه شمالاً وجنوباً عمارة وافرة لفرط الحرارة، ولم يكن حوالي القطبين عمارة أصلاً لفرط البرودة، وقع معظم العمارة في الربع المسكون بين ما يجاوز عشر درجات في العرض عن خط الاستواء إلى أن يبلغ العرض قريب خمسين، فقسم أهل الصناعة هذا القدر سبعة أقسام في العرض حسب ما ظهر لهم من تفاوت تشابه الأحوال في الحر والبرد، فاعتبروا في الطول الامتداد من المشرق إلى المغرب، وفي العرض تفاضل نصف ساعة في مقادير النهار الأطول أعني نهار كون الشمس في الانقلاب الصيفي، وكل من الأقاليم ينحصر بين نصفي مدارين موازيين لخط الاستواء أشبه شيء بأنصاف
He said: And they called from the meridian and what is between the zenith direction of the town and the celestial equator the latitude of the town, and from the celestial equator what is the meridian of the town and the meridian of the furthest habitation in the west the longitude of the town. The latitude of the town is an arc of the meridian between the celestial equator and the pole of the horizon of the town, i.e., the zenith, and it necessarily equals what is between the horizon of the town and the pole of the celestial equator, i.e., the elevation of the pole. So at the horizon of the equator, there is no latitude for the town because the line from the center of the world passing through the two zeniths of the head and the foot falls on the celestial equator and does not depart from it. At the horizon coinciding with the celestial equator, the latitude is at its maximum, i.e., ninety. In other cases, the town has a latitude equal to the inclination of the horizon from the celestial equator. So if we take the altitude of the sun at midday on the vernal or autumnal equinox and subtract it from ninety, the remainder is the latitude of the town. As for the longitude of the town, it is an arc of the day between the meridian of the town and the meridian of the furthest habitation in the west. The Greeks took the west as baseline because it was the closest of the two ends of habitation to them. The furthest habitation according to some is the western sea coast, and according to Ptolemy it is the eternal islands extending into the sea, with ten degrees between them, which is close to two hundred and twenty parasangs. He said: And they divided the inhabited region into seven zones parallel to the celestial equator extending from east to west, calling them the seven climes. Since there was not abundant habitation on the equator and its vicinity north and south due to excessive heat, and there was no habitation at all around the poles due to extreme cold, most habitation occurred in the inhabited quarter between what exceeds ten degrees in latitude from the equator until the latitude reaches about fifty. So the experts of the craft divided this amount into seven divisions in latitude according to what appeared to them of the variation in similarity of conditions in heat and cold. They considered in longitude the extension from east to west, and in latitude the difference of half an hour in the amounts of the longest day, i.e., the day when the sun is at the summer solstice. And each of the climes is bounded between two semicircles parallel to the equator, resembling semicircles
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage defines latitude and longitude and then explains the division of the inhabited world into seven climes. It begins by stating how latitude and longitude are derived from the meridian: latitude is the arc between the celestial equator and the zenith of the town, which equals the elevation of the pole. At the equator, latitude is zero; at the pole, it is ninety degrees. Latitude is calculated by measuring the sun's altitude at noon on an equinox and subtracting it from ninety. Longitude is the arc between the town's meridian and the meridian of the westernmost inhabited point; the Greeks used the western boundary because it was closer to them, with varying definitions (the western sea shore or Ptolemy's 'eternal islands'). The passage then transitions to the seven climes: because excessive heat near the equator and extreme cold near the poles prevent habitation, most of the inhabited world lies between roughly ten and fifty degrees latitude. Scholars divided this band into seven zones (aqalim) based on differences in climate and the duration of the longest day (summer solstice). Each clime is bounded by two parallel circles resembling semicircles. The passage ends mid-sentence but provides the key rationale and method.

Key Terms
الأقاليم السبعة
الانقلاب الصيفي
معدل النهار
العرض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The seven climes are political or administrative regions.
Correction: They are climate zones based on latitude and day length, not political divisions.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The seven climes are climate zones dividing the habitable band between 10° and 50° latitude by half-hour differences in the summer solstice day length.

The Seven Climes: Latitude Divisions of the Inhabited World
Explains the division of the inhabited world into seven climes and their latitude boundaries.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how medieval scholars divided the inhabited world into seven climes based on latitude and day length.

Core Idea
The seven climes are defined by half-hour differences in the longest day.

This passage from Sharh al-Maqasid explains the classical Islamic geographical division of the inhabited world into seven climes. The scholars used astronomical observations, specifically the length of the longest day at the summer solstice, to define these latitudinal bands. Let's explore how they determined the boundaries and why certain latitudes were excluded.

Guided Path
1
Understand the rationale
Read why habitation is limited between latitudes 10° and 50° due to extreme heat near the equator and extreme cold near the poles.
The 'inhabited quarter' is the focus, not the entire globe.
2
Learn the method
Notice that the divisions are based on half-hour increments in the length of the longest day (summer solstice). Each clime corresponds to a half-hour difference.
This makes the division astronomical rather than purely geographical.
3
Memorize the clime boundaries
Study the precise starting latitudes for each clime, from 12 2/3° for the first to 50 1/3° for the end of the seventh.
Some scholars start the first clime at the equator itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وقسموا المعمورة سبع قطاع موازية لمعدل النهار ممتدة من المشرق إلى المغرب سموها الأقاليم السبعة. لما لم يكن على خط الاستواء وما يدانيه شمالاً وجنوباً عمارة وافرة لفرط الحرارة، ولم يكن حوالي القطبين عمارة أصلاً لفرط البرودة، وقع معظم العمارة في الربع المسكون بين ما يجاوز عشر درجات في العرض عن خط الاستواء إلى أن يبلغ العرض قريب خمسين، فقسم أهل الصناعة هذا القدر سبعة أقسام في العرض حسب ما ظهر لهم من تفاوت تشابه الأحوال في الحر والبرد، فاعتبروا في الطول الامتداد من المشرق إلى المغرب، وفي العرض تفاضل نصف ساعة في مقادير النهار الأطول أعني نهار كون الشمس في الانقلاب الصيفي، وكل من الأقاليم ينحصر بين نصفي مدارين موازيين لخط الاستواء أشبه شيء بأنصاف الدفوف ولا محالة يكون أحد طرفيه وهو الشمالي أضيق، ومبدأ الإقليم الأول حيث العرض اثنا عشر درجة وثلثا درجة والثاني حيث العرض عشرون وربع وخمس، والثالث حيث العرض سبع وعشرون ونصف والرابع حيث العرض ثلاث وثلاثون ونصف وثمن، والخامس حيث العرض تسع وثلاثون إلا عشراً، والسادس حيث العرض ثلاث وأربعون وربع وثمن، والسابع حيث العرض سبع وأربعون وخمس، وآخره حيث العرض خمسون وثلث. ومنهم من جعل مبدأ الأول خط الاستواء، وآخر السابع منتهى العمارة.
He said: And they divided the inhabited world into seven strips parallel to the equator, extending from east to west, calling them the seven climes. Since there is no abundant habitation on the equator and near it north and south because of extreme heat, and there is no habitation at all near the poles because of extreme cold, most of the habitation falls in the inhabited quarter between that which exceeds ten degrees in latitude from the equator until the latitude reaches near fifty. So the people of the craft divided this extent into seven divisions in latitude according to what appeared to them of the differences in similarity of conditions in heat and cold. They considered in longitude the extension from east to west, and in latitude the difference of half an hour in the lengths of the longest day, i.e., the day of the sun being at the summer solstice. Each of the climes is confined between two half-circles parallel to the equator, very similar to half of the دفوف (tambourines?), and inevitably one of its two ends, the northern, is narrower. The beginning of the first clime is where the latitude is twelve and two-thirds degrees; the second where the latitude is twenty and a quarter and a fifth; the third where the latitude is twenty-seven and a half; the fourth where the latitude is thirty-three and a half and an eighth; the fifth where the latitude is thirty-nine minus a tenth; the sixth where the latitude is forty-three and a quarter and an eighth; the seventh where the latitude is forty-seven and a fifth; and its end where the latitude is fifty and a third. And some of them made the beginning of the first [clime] the equator, and the end of the seventh the limit of habitation.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage classifies the inhabited world into seven climes (أقاليم) based on latitude. It begins by stating that the scholars divided the inhabited world into seven strips parallel to the equator, called climes. The reason for limiting habitation to between latitudes 10° and 50° is extreme heat near the equator and extreme cold near the poles. The climes are defined by differences in half an hour in the length of the longest day (summer solstice). Each clime is bounded by two parallel circles; the northern boundary is narrower. The author then lists the precise latitudes for the start of each clime, from 12 2/3° for the first up to 50 1/3° for the end of the seventh. Some scholars, however, start the first clime from the equator itself and end the seventh at the limit of habitation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The climes are modern political or climate zones based on temperature alone.
Correction: The climes are defined by astronomical day length differences (half-hour increments) at the summer solstice, not by modern Köppen climate classification.

Celestial Motions at Different Latitudes
Describes celestial motions at equator, pole, and inclined horizons.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the apparent rotation of the celestial sphere differs at the equator, the pole, and inclined horizons, and how this affects day length and seasons.

Core Idea
The sky rotates like a wheel at the equator, like a millstone at the pole, and like a hanging at intermediate latitudes.

In this passage, the author explains three distinct patterns of celestial rotation that depend on the observer's latitude. These patterns follow from the geometry of the celestial sphere relative to the local horizon. Understanding them helps explain why day length varies with latitude and season.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the English translation. Let the author's descriptions of the three rotations sink in before examining details.
Note the three key terms: دولابي, رحوي, حمائلي.
2
Examine the equator description
The author says rotation is 'dolabiy' (wheel-like), day and night always equal, sun overhead at equinoxes (summer) and distant at solstices (winter), resulting in eight seasons.
The 'eight seasons' refer to two equinoxes, two solstices, and their intermediates.
3
Examine the pole description
At latitude 90°, rotation is 'rahwiy' (millstone-like), half the sky always visible, half always hidden, so the year is one day and one night.
This is an idealized description; in practice, the sun's declination causes variation.
4
Examine inclined horizons
At intermediate latitudes, rotation is 'hamailiy' (hanging-like). The visible arcs of northern circles are larger when the latitude is northern, causing longer days when the sun is in northern signs and shorter days in southern signs.
The degree of variation depends on the latitude difference.
5
Reflect on the geometry
The author notes that at the equator, the daily circles cut the horizon at angles. Consider why this leads to the wheel-like rotation and equal day/night.
This geometric insight connects the abstract model to observed phenomena.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ففي خط الاستواء يكون دور الفلك دولابياً، والليل والنهار متساويان أبداً، ويسامت الشمس رءوسهم في الاعتدالين، وهو صيف، ويبعد في الانقلابين وهو شتاء، فيكون الفصول ثمانية، وفي عرض تسعين يكون الدور رحوياً، ونصف الفلك ظاهراً أبداً، والنصف خفياً، والسنة يوماً وليلة وفي الآفاق الماثلة يكون الدور حمائلياً، والقسي الظاهرة من المدارات الشمالية أعظم، إذا كان العرض شمالياً، فيكون النهار أطول إذا كان الشمس في البروج الشمالية، وبالعكس في الجنوبية وبحسب تفاوت العروض يكون تفاضل القسي، وتفاوت الليل والنهار. إشارة إلى نبذ من خواص المواضع التي لا عرض بها، وإلى التي لها عرض، أما البقاع التي لا عرض لها، لكونها على خط الاستواء، فدور الفلك هناك يكون دولابياً، لأن سطوح جميع المدارات اليومية، تقطع سطح الأفق على زوايا
He said: At the equator, the rotation of the celestial sphere is like a wheel (dolabiy), and night and day are always equal. The sun passes directly overhead at the equinoxes—this is summer—and it distances itself at the solstices—this is winter—so there are eight seasons. At latitude ninety [the pole], the rotation is like a millstone (rahwiy), half of the celestial sphere is always visible and half hidden, and the year is a single day and night. At inclined horizons, the rotation is like a hanging (hamailiy), and the visible arcs from the northern circles are greater if the latitude is northern, so the day is longer when the sun is in the northern signs, and the opposite in the southern. And according to the differences in latitudes, there are differences in the arcs and variations in night and day. An indication of some of the properties of places with no latitude and those with latitude: As for places with no latitude, because they are on the equator, the rotation of the celestial sphere there is like a wheel, because the surfaces of all the daily circles cut the plane of the horizon at angles...
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage explains the celestial motions at different latitudes. It begins by describing the equator: the rotation is 'dolabiy' (wheel-like), meaning the celestial equator is perpendicular to the horizon, so day and night are always equal. The sun passes overhead at equinoxes (summer) and is farthest at solstices (winter), resulting in eight seasons. At the pole (latitude 90°), the rotation is 'rahwiy' (millstone-like), with the celestial equator parallel to the horizon. Half the sky is always visible, half always hidden, so the year is one day and one night. At inclined horizons (intermediate latitudes), the rotation is 'hamailiy' (hanging), with the visible arcs of northern circles being larger when the latitude is northern, causing longer days in summer and shorter in winter. The author then restates that at the equator, the daily circles cut the horizon at angles, which explains the equatorial rotation. The passage ends abruptly, likely continuing the explanation.

Key Terms

دور رحوي
دور حمائلي
خط الاستواء
عرض تسعين
الاعتدالين
الانقلابين
الفصول ثمانية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The 'eight seasons' might be misunderstood as the modern four seasons split into eight equal parts.
Correction: The eight seasons refer to the two equinoxes, two solstices, and the four intermediate points between them, not eight meteorological seasons.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The apparent rotation of the sky varies with latitude: wheel-like at the equator, millstone-like at the pole, and hanging-like at intermediate latitudes, affecting day length and seasons.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The 'hanging' rotation at intermediate latitudes causes unequal day lengths. If you measured your life not by hours but by closeness to Allah, do you have seasons of spiritual 'summer' and 'winter'? What one practice could you start today to even out your seasons?

The Seven Climes and Their Latitudes
Enumeration of the seven climes with their latitudinal boundaries

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the latitudinal boundaries of the seven climes as defined in classical Islamic geography.

Core Idea
Latitude, not climate, defines the seven climes.

In this passage, the author enumerates the seven climes (climates) with precise latitudinal boundaries. This classification was used by medieval geographers to divide the inhabited world. Understanding these boundaries helps us appreciate how pre-modern scholars mapped the earth.

1
Read the passage

The numbers are fractions of degrees.

Identify the seven climes

3

This shows scholarly disagreement.
4
Reflect on the purpose

ومبدأ الإقليم الأول حيث العرض اثنا عشر درجة وثلثا درجة والثاني حيث العرض عشرون وربع وخمس، والثالث حيث العرض سبع وعشرون ونصف والرابع حيث العرض ثلاث وثلاثون ونصف وثمن، والخامس حيث العرض تسع وثلاثون إلا عشراً، والسادس حيث العرض ثلاث وأربعون وربع وثمن، والسابع حيث العرض سبع وأربعون وخمس، وآخره حيث العرض خمسون وثلث. ومنهم من جعل مبدأ الأول خط الاستواء، وآخر السابع منتهى العمارة.

This passage is an enumeration of the seven climes (climates) with their latitudinal boundaries. Equatorial Rotation and Day-Night Equality
Explanation of equatorial rotation and day-night equality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the celestial rotation at the equator resembles a wheel and why day and night are always equal there, with only imperceptible variations due to the sun's motion.

Core Idea
At the equator, the horizon bisects all daily orbits, making day and night perpetually equal.

The great scholar al-Sanusi begins by describing the unique celestial mechanics of the equator. He explains that the rotation of the heavens there is like a wheel, because the planes of daily orbits intersect the horizon at right angles. This leads to the remarkable property of equal day and night throughout the year, with only tiny, unobservable differences caused by the sun's varying speed in its epicycle.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Notice the concise statement followed by the detailed reasoning. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
The passage begins with a quote from the matn.
2
Understand the wheel simile
Al-Sanusi compares the celestial sphere to a wheel (dulab) cutting water. Visualize the daily orbits intersecting the horizon at right angles.
This geometric relation is key to the equality of day and night.
3
Grasp the equality of day and night
The horizon bisects all daily orbits, so the visible day arc equals the hidden night arc.
This holds true at all times at the equator.
4
Consider the imperceptible variations
Al-Sanusi explains that the sun's epicycle motion causes slight differences in day length, but these are negligible.
The apogee/perigee difference in solar motion is too small to be observed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال: (ففي خط الاستواء يكون دور الفلك دولابياً، والليل والنهار متساويان أبداً، ويسامت الشمس رءوسهم في الاعتدالين، وهو صيف، ويبعد في الانقلابين وهو شتاء، فيكون الفصول ثمانية). إشارة إلى نبذ من خواص المواضع التي لا عرض بها، وإلى التي لها عرض، أما البقاع التي لا عرض لها، لكونها على خط الاستواء، فدور الفلك هناك يكون دولابياً، لأن سطوح جميع المدارات اليومية، تقطع سطح الأفق على زوايا قائمة، كما تقطع الدولاب سطح الماء، ويكون الليل والنهار في جميع الأوقات متساويين، لأن الأفق ينصف جميع المدارات اليومية، فيكون الظاهر أعني قوس النهار مساوياً للخفي أعني قوس الليل. فإن كان تفاوت، كان بسبب اختلاف المسير بسبب الحركة الثانية مثلاً إذا كانت الشمس بالنهار في النصف الأوجي من فلكها الخارج، كانت حركتها الثانية أعني التي من المغرب إلى المشرق أبطأ، فتديرها الحركة الأولى من المشرق إلى المغرب أسرع، وإذا انتقلت بالليل إلى النصف الحضيضي كانت الحركة الثانية أسرع، فتعيدها الحركة الأولى أبطأ، فتتفاوت الحركتان في نصفي مدار ذلك اليوم، لكن ذلك غير محسوس، وتسامت الشمس رءوسهم في السنة مرتين مرة في اعتدال رأس الحمل، ومرة في رأس الميزان، لأن مدار الشمس حينئذ هو المعدل المار بسمت رؤسهم، ويبعد غاية البعد مرتين مرة في انقلاب رأس السرطان، وأخرى في انقلاب رأس الجدي، ولكون غاية القرب مبدأ الصيف، وغاية البعد مبدأ الشتاء يكون لهم صيفان، وشتاءان وبين كل صيف وشتاء خريف وبين كل شتاء وصيف ربيع، فتكون فصولهم ثمانية، كل منها شهراً ونصفاً تقريباً.
He said: 'At the equator, the rotation of the celestial sphere is like that of a wheel, and night and day are always equal, and the sun is overhead at the two equinoxes, which is summer, and it is distant at the two solstices, which is winter, so the seasons are eight.' Indication of some properties of places that have no latitude, and of those that have latitude. As for the regions that have no latitude, because they are on the equator, the rotation of the celestial sphere there is like a wheel, because the planes of all daily orbits intersect the plane of the horizon at right angles, just as a wheel cuts the surface of water, and night and day at all times are equal, because the horizon bisects all daily orbits, so the visible, meaning the arc of day, is equal to the hidden, meaning the arc of night. If there is inequality, it is due to difference in motion because of the second motion; for example, if the sun is in the daytime in the apogee half of its epicycle, its second motion, that is from west to east, is slower, so the first motion from east to west moves it faster, and when it moves at night to the perigee half, the second motion is faster, so the first motion moves it slower, so the two motions differ in the two halves of the orbit of that day, but that is imperceptible. And the sun is overhead twice a year, once at the equinox of Aries, and once at the equinox of Libra, because the sun's orbit then is the celestial equator passing through their zenith, and it is at maximum distance twice, once at the solstice of Cancer, and once at the solstice of Capricorn. And because the point of closest approach is the beginning of summer, and the point of farthest distance is the beginning of winter, they have two summers and two winters, and between each summer and winter is autumn, and between each winter and summer is spring, so their seasons are eight, each approximately a month and a half.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage begins by quoting the matn regarding the equator, then provides a detailed explanation. The matn states that at the equator, the celestial sphere's rotation is like a wheel, day and night are always equal, the sun is overhead at the equinoxes (considered summer) and distant at the solstices (considered winter), resulting in eight seasons. The commentary then explains the reason for the wheel-like rotation: the daily orbital planes intersect the horizon at right angles, similar to a wheel cutting water. It also notes that any slight inequality in day and night length is due to the sun's motion in its epicycle—specifically the difference between the apogee and perigee velocities—but such differences are imperceptible. The passage then details the sun's annual path: it is overhead at the two equinoxes (Aries and Libra) and at maximum distance at the two solstices (Cancer and Capricorn). This produces two summers (at the closest approach), two winters (at the farthest distance), and intermediate autumns and springs, making eight seasons, each approximately 45 days.

Key Terms
خط الاستواء
دولابي
المدارات اليومية
الأفق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think day and night are exactly equal at the equator at all times without any variation.
Correction: The passage explains that tiny variations occur due to the sun's epicycle motion, though they are imperceptible.

Checkpoint
According to al-Sanusi, why is the rotation of the celestial sphere at the equator compared to a wheel?
A) Because the sun appears to roll across the sky.
B) Because the daily orbital planes intersect the horizon at right angles.
C) Because the equator is a circle.
D) Because the sun moves fastest at the equator.

Key Takeaway
At the equator, the horizon bisects all daily orbits, resulting in nearly equal day and night throughout the year.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you ponder the precise geometry that ensures constant equality of day and night at the equator, do you not feel a sense of awe at the meticulous planning of your Creator? How often do you take a moment to recognize His perfect order in the universe, and what change would be required for you to live with constant awareness of His design?
?
The passage mentions a hidden inequality in the heavens that is imperceptible to you. In your own life, are there subtle imbalances in your worship, character, or relationships that you overlook because they are not immediately obvious? What would it take for you to seek out and correct these hidden flaws with the same dedication the scholars use to uncover celestial motions?
?
If the rotation of the heavens operates with such flawless precision, what does that demand of your own actions and intentions? Are your days and nights equally devoted to your Lord, or is there an imperceptible inequality that you have allowed? Make a concrete commitment today to bring more balance to your spiritual life.

Sun Positions and Eight Seasons at the Equator
Explanation of the sun's positions and eight seasons at the equator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the equator experiences two summers, two winters, and eight distinct seasons based on the sun's position relative to the equinoxes and solstices.

Core Idea
The sun passes overhead twice a year at the equator, creating two summers and two winters, hence eight seasons.

Al-Sanusi now turns to the sun's annual journey as seen from the equator. Because the sun is directly overhead at the equinoxes and farthest away at the solstices, the equatorial region experiences two summers (at the equinoxes) and two winters (at the solstices). With the transitions of autumn and spring between each, the total number of seasons comes to eight, each lasting about a month and a half.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Focus on the sun's positions: overhead at equinoxes, distant at solstices.
The equinoxes mark the start of summer, not spring as in temperate zones.
2
Understand the seasonal logic
Closest approach (overhead) = summer, farthest distance = winter. Two each gives eight seasons.
This is due to the sun's annual motion north and south of the equator.
3
Note the duration
Each season is about a month and a half (45 days).
Eight seasons of 45 days each total 360 days, approximately a year.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Celestial Sphere at the North Pole
Description of the North Pole's celestial rotation and visibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the unique celestial geometry at the North Pole, where the rotation is millstone-like, the celestial equator coincides with the horizon, and the year consists of one day and one night.

Core Idea
At the pole, the sky rotates like a millstone around a vertical axis.

This lesson explores a fascinating astronomical scenario: what happens to the celestial sphere at the North Pole (latitude 90°)? The classical text describes how the rotation becomes completely horizontal, half the sky is always visible, and the year reduces to a single day and night. This sets the stage for understanding how the heavens behave at extreme latitudes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then its English translation. Notice the specific terms used for rotation and visibility.
The Arabic term 'رحوي' (millstone-like) is key to visualizing the motion.
2
Identify the key features
List the three characteristics the passage gives: rotation type, visibility of halves, and year length. Then note the explanation about the celestial equator being the horizon.
These features are directly observable at the North Pole.
3
Visualize the geometry
Imagine standing at the North Pole: the north celestial pole is directly overhead, so the celestial equator lies on the horizon. Stars and the sun circle parallel to the horizon, never rising or setting but just revolving.
This explains why half the sphere is always above and half below.
4
Connect to the misconception
Consider the common misunderstanding that day and night are exactly six months each. The passage implies an annual cycle of one daylight and one darkness, but the actual timing is gradual.
The text says 'the year is a day and a night' – this is a simplified description.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي عرض تسعين يكون الدور رحوياً، ونصف الفلك ظاهراً أبداً، والنصف خفياً، والسنة يوماً وليلة. وأما في عرض تسعين، أعني حيث يكون قطب العالم على سمت الرأس، فدور الفلك يكون رحوياً لكون معدل النهار هو الأفق، ولا يبقى في الأفق مشرق ولا مغرب متميزين، بل في جميع
And at latitude ninety, the rotation is like that of a millstone, and half of the celestial sphere is always visible, and half hidden, and the year is a day and a night. As for at latitude ninety, that is where the pole of the world is at the zenith, the rotation of the celestial sphere is like that of a millstone because the celestial equator is the horizon, and there remains in the horizon no distinct east or west, but in all
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage discusses the North Pole (latitude 90°). The matn states that at this latitude, the rotation is like a millstone (رحي), half the celestial sphere is always visible, half always hidden, and the year consists of one day and one night (referring to the sun's continuous visibility for half the year and continuous darkness for the other half). The commentary then explains that at the pole, the pole of the world is at the zenith, and the celestial equator coincides with the horizon. Consequently, there is no distinct east or west on the horizon; all directions are effectively south (or north). The text is cut off, but it likely continues to elaborate on the implications.

Key Terms

رحوي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that at the North Pole, the sun is always visible for exactly six months and then invisible for six months, with distinct day-night cycles.
Correction: The passage simplifies by saying 'the year is a day and a night', but the actual transition is gradual; at the pole, the sun is above the horizon for about six months and below for about six months, but the rotation of the sphere is continuous and the horizon aligns with the celestial equator.

Key Takeaway
At the North Pole, the celestial equator lies on the horizon, causing the sphere to rotate horizontally, with half always visible and the year consisting of one continuous day and night.

Take a moment to thank Him for the regular alternation of day and night that keeps your life stable. Will you make it a habit to reflect on this when you see the sun rise or set?
